CHAIRMAN\n\n\nSIDDHARTH INSTITUTE OF ENGINEERING & TECHNOLOGY\n\n\nFULLY SOLAR ENERGY POWERED INSTITUTE\n\n\nSiddharth Institute of Engineering & Technology (SIETK) is an emerging center for excellence in Engineering & Management education, boast of energetic & experienced faculty, successful students, great infrastructure and excellent placements record. The management encourages the students and the faculty to “Dare to Dream and Strive to Achieve”. The institutes are indeed “dream come true” for many aspiring youngsters from rural areas in Chittoor District and Southern Andhra Pradesh.\n\nThe institution, it is believed that “Change is the only constant thing”. The infrastructure and equipment are constantly upgraded, providing opportunities to the faculty and the students to enhance their skills continuously. The institutions aim at preparing the students to be great problem solvers, project leaders, communicators, and ethical citizens of a global community.\n\nEstablished in 2001 (SIETK) in a sprawling 30-acre campus amid beautiful hill range of the Eastern Ghats, the institutions are located in Puttur town and are very proximate to Narayanavanam, a holy place, where Lord Venkateswara has married Goddess Padmavathi. The institutions are 22kms from Tirupati airport and are well connected by rail and road (Tirupati – Chennai highway).The institutions are promoted by Jaya Educational Society, founded and professionally run by distinguished academicians, medical professionals and technocrats belonging to Chittoor District in Andhra Pradesh.\n\n# Phenomenal Growth & Trust\n\nThe institutions have achieved remarkable growth since their inception and have grown from strength to strength under the dynamic and innovative leadership of the Chairman, Dr. K. Ashok Raju. In addition to Graduate Engineering (B.Tech.), the institutions have been approved to run Post-graduate (M.Tech - nine specializations, MCA & MBA) and Diploma programmes. The total intake of students for SIETK has gone up from 180 in 2001 to 1842 in 2017, a testimony of abundant trust placed by the students and the parents in these institutions.\n\n# Well Accredited and Competing with Global Standards\n\nSiddharth Institute of Engineering & Technology has received NBA (National Board of Accreditations) accreditation for five programmes and has been accredited by NAAC with ‘A’ grade.\n\nInnovation and Entrepreneurship division of Department of Science and Technology, Government of India has established prestigious incubation centre in Siddharth with registered name “Society for Siddharth International Incubation Centre” to support technology based start-ups, potential technology ideas and innovations. Siddharth International Incubation Centre already submitted 15 innovative ideas to Government of India and another 115 start-ups in pipeline. One of the US based company launching shortly in Siddharth.\n\n\n\nASSOCHAM (The Associated Chambers of Commerce and Industry of India) recognized the Siddharth Institute of Engineering and Technology as one among the “Best Engineering Colleges in South India” for excellence in education in 2013.\n\n\n\nSIETK’s innovative approach to educating students is an Ecosystem-based Systems Integration and Networking (EbSIN) model. We seek to engage experts from around the world on mutual projects, thus allowing our students to acquire real-life, live, project based experiential learning.\n\n\n**Our student Miss. J. Hemalatha (III CSE) has been selected as UIF by STANDFORD UNIVERSITY through Google.**\n\nUnder the visionary leadership of the chairman, the institutions compete with global standards. An important step towards the same is an MOU with University of Massachusetts Lowell, USA that enables exchange of students and faculty among the institutions, joint projects, research, etc.\n\n\nThe institutions are also Microsoft Ed-Vantage Platinum level campuses with Microsoft Innovation Centre in place. This association with Microsoft is to encourage the students to get certified on Microsoft technologies and get an edge over their competition. IBM Center of Excellence has trained the students in the following domains Cloud computing, Big Data (Hadoop) and Mobile application development.\n\n\nWith Association of Andhra Pradesh State skill development Centre (APSSDC), SIEMENS company established following 07 laboratories with world class standards. Design CBT lab, Auto Two Wheeler lab, Auto Four Wheeler Lab, Electrical Home Lab, Electrical RAC lab, Electronics Home Lab and Electronics ICT Lab.\n\n\n\n# Physical Infrastructure - Highlights\n\n**In a nut shell, following are the highlights of the institutions:**\n\nAesthetically designed buildings with spacious, well-ventilated and well-furnished classrooms and laboratories.\n\nWell-equipped laboratories with the latest equipment and continuously upgraded based on requirements.\n\nE-learning classrooms in every department to use technology and modern teaching methods to train the students more effectively.\n\nAir-conditioned library with latest collection of volumes. In addition, an exclusive Digital Library.\n\nFour air-conditioned seminar halls with capacities of 500 and 300, with LCD projectors and sound systems for in-house training sessions and association activities.\n\n4000-capacity A/C auditorium with world class Audio and Video systems for major activities such as off-campus selections, seminars, competitions, annual functions and celebrations.\n\nDedicated infrastructure to host in-campus selection drives.\n\nAir-conditioned computer labs with brand new computers with latest configuration.\n\nWi-Fi all over the campus.\n\nExclusive hostels for girls and boys with modern facilities.\n\nA hygienic canteen within the campus catering to the needs of the students and the staff at concessional prices.\n\nMineral water plants throughout the campus.\n\nSpacious playgrounds for extra-curricular development of the students.\n\n\n\n# Other Highlights\n\nThe Research and Development (R&D) cell organizes industrial visits/tours to help the students gain practical knowledge of work situations in their respective branches and there by acquire hands - on – experience.\n\nEntrepreneurship Development Cell undertakes training programs enabling promising students to emerge as prospective entrepreneurs.\nSpecial care is taken to focus on individual student by periodical personal counselling with thrust on discipline, attendance and academic progress.\n\nOur colleges have got Institutional Membership of “The Indian Society for Technical Education” and also ISTE Students Chapter.\nWe are ISO 9001: 2008certified institutions.\n\n\n## IMPORTANT LINKS\n\n[Audit Statement](https://sietk.org/downloads/Audit%20Statements#.pdf)\n[AICTE Approvals 2025-26](https://sietk.org/AICTE/2025-26.pdf)\n[AICTE framing of\nacademic policy, approval of courses, regulations, syllabi. Academic Council shall propose\nways and means to maintain quality norms. The Council will involve faculty at all levels and\nalso experts from outside, including representatives of the institution and the government. The\ndecisions taken by the Academic Council will not be subject to any further ratification by the\nAcademic Council or other statutory bodies of the institution. The decisions of the Academic\ncouncil are to be placed before the Governing Body for final approval and changes, if any, by its member secretary.\n\n\n# Academic Council Members\n\n| S.No | Name of the Member | Designation/Organization | Role in Academic Council |\n| --- | --- | --- | --- |\n| 1 | Dr. K. {
  "markdown": "# SIDDHARTH INSTITUTE OF ENGINEERING & TECHNOLOGY:: PUTTUR (AUTONOMOUS)\n\nSiddharth Nagar, Narayanavanam Road – 517583\n\n# QUESTION BANK (DESCRIPTIVE)\n\nSubject with Code: Agricultural Process Engineering(19AG0707) Course & Branch: B.Tech-AGE Year &Sem: III-B.Tech &I-Sem Regulation: R19\n\n# UNIT – I PHYSICAL CHARACTERISTICS OF DIFFERENT FOOD GRAINS AND RHEOLOGY\n\n|     |     |     |     |     |\n| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |\n| 1. | a. | Write the classification and importance of Physical & Mechanical properties ofbiological materials. | \\[L1\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n| b. | Give the classification and importance of Thermal and Electrical properties ofbiological materials. | \\[L1\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n| 2. | a. | Explain projected area method for measurement of size with neat sketch. | \\[L2\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n| b. | Define specific gravity. List out the methods for determination of specificgravity and explain Specific gravity balance (used for small fruits). | \\[L1\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n| 3. | a. | Briefly explain the importance of engineering properties of biomaterialmaterials. | \\[L2\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n|  | b. | Write the applications of Aero-hydrodynamic, Frictional and Optical propertiesof biological materials. | \\[L1\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n| 4. | a. | Explain roundness, roundness ratio and sphericity with suitable equations andneat sketch. | \\[L2\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n|  | b. | Define bulk density, true density, apparent density with related expressions. | \\[L1\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n| 5. | a. | Define porosity. Explain the method for determination of porosity with neatsketch. | \\[L2\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[8M\\] |\n| b. | Tank 2 of the apparatus is filled with a sample of dry shelled corn to a bulkdensity of 752.86kg/m3. The pressure readings were P1=0.38m and P3=0.26m.Find the porosity of the corn. | \\[L3\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[4M\\] |\n| 6. | a. | Explain the platform scale for measurement of volume, density and specificgravity of large objects with neat sketch. | \\[L2\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n| b. | Define surface area. Explain the methods for determination of the surface are ofleaf & stalk, fruits & vegetables, Cereals, pulses and oil seeds. | \\[L2\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n| 7. | − | Explain the possible force-deformation curve for an agricultural product. | \\[L2\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[12M\\] |\n| 8. | − | List out the rheological models and derive kelvin model with related equations. | \\[L4\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[12M\\] |\n| 9. | a. | Define rheology. Write the classification, importance and application ofrheological properties. | \\[L1\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[8M\\] |\n| − | b. | Define stress relaxation, retardation time and creep with diagrams. | \\[L1\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[4M\\] |\n| 10. | a. | Explain the Toughness, Resilience and Stiffness with neat sketch. | \\[L2\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n| − | b. | List out and explain the Non Newtonian fluids with graphical representation. | \\[L2\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n\nUNIT-IIFRICTIONAL, AERODYNAMIC, ELECTRICAL AND THERMAL PROPERTIES\n\n|     |     |     |     |     |\n| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |\n| 1. | a. | Deline Inction. Explain types of Iniction and wnite equation for Inctional forcewith neat sketch. | \\[LT\\]\\[C02\\] | \\[0M\\] |\n| b. | Define coefficient of friction and explain the experimental setup formeasurement of it. | \\[L1\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n| 2. | a. | Define angle of internal friction and list out the factors effecting frictional force. | \\[L2\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[5M\\] |\n| b. | Explain the Experimental set up for coefficient of internal friction with neatsketch | \\[L2\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[7M\\] |\n| 3. | a. | Explain the method for determination of angle of repose of the food grains withneat sketch. | \\[L2\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n| b. | Explain Rolling resistance with neat sketch. | \\[L2\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n| 4. | a. | Explain the role of aerodynamic properties in food processing | \\[L2\\]\\[CO2\\] | \\[6M\\] |\n|  | b. | What is a drag coefficient? The department was established in 2004 with 60 UG students Intake and now running with 120 Intake.\n\nThe PG course Thermal Engineering has started in the year 2012 with an Intake of 18. The department is headed by Dr.S.SUNIL KUMAR REDDY who has more than 26 years of teaching experience. The Department is rich in term of faculty members who has vast teaching, Industrial and Research experience with an average teaching experience of 10 years. The Department has 12 members with Ph.D and 07 pursuing their research in various prestigious Universities.\n\n\n\nResearch Center has been sanctioned by Jawaharlal Technological University, Anantapur. The faculty published more than 300 papers in National and International Conferences/Journals. The major areas of research include Alternate Fuels, Combustion, Composite materials, Solar Energy etc.,\n\n\n\nThe Department has established Industry Academia Partnership with various manufacturing Industries in which the students will get trained on latest technology. Further the department in collaboration with Andhra Pradesh State Skill Development Corporation (APSSDC) established various labs i.e Design CBT lab, Refrigeration & Air Conditioning Lab, Automobile 2 wheeler and 4 wheeler labs. Dassault 3D experience lab is an asset for the department. In all these labs the students will be provided hands on experience to make them Industry ready candidate for various design and manufacturing companies. These infra facilities will cater the needs of UG and PG students.\n\n\n\nThe department is also having an agreement with IIT Tirupati, with which the faculty can obtain mentorship from them for their research projects. It consists of separate department library with an around 1000 books and the students will utilize this along with college central library.\n\n\n\nThe Department has conventional and research laboratories. The major drafting, modeling software in the department are AUTOCAD, CATIA, DELMIA, SILMIA, SOLID EDGE, etc.\n\n\n\nThe faculty inculcates discipline and responsibility among the students along with regular teaching. The department prepared advanced curriculum to students with the help of Industrial people.\n\n\n\n# VISION & MISSION OF THE DEPARTMENT\n\n## Vision\n\nTo produce competent, ethical mechanical engineering professionals capable of working worldwide and transforming society for a better life with their research-based technology and entrepreneurial skills.\n\n\n## Mission\n\nThe primary mission of the Department of Mechanical Engineering is to impart high class education to the students by its three tenets to serve the society:\n\nThe mission of the Department of Mechanical Engineering has three tenets :\n\n**M1 :** Providing extensive knowledge on Mechanical Engineering and allied subjects with ethical values by well-experienced faculty.\n\n\n**M2 :** Developing entrepreneurial and research-oriented skills to produce novel products of economic viability.\n\n\n**M3 :** Creating opportunities for industrial training to understand industry related issues and advanced technologies in the workplace.\n\n\nPEO\n\nThe Program Educational Objectives of the Mechanical Engineering are:\n\n\n**PEO1:** Graduates with their profound knowledge of science and engineering fundamentals, are capable of identifying and providing innovative solutions to complex mechanical engineering designs and real-time problems, with a strong emphasis on environmental sustainability.\n\n\n**PEO2:** Graduates become successful professionals or entrepreneurs with ethical values, good communication skills, and ability to work in a team.\n\n\n**PEO3:** Graduates have the potential to pursue higher education and research with a commitment to lifelong learning, and work in industries adapting to evolving professional challenges.\n\n\nPO'S\n\nThe following are the program outcomes of Engineering Graduates:\n\n\n**PO1:** Engineering knowledge: Apply the knowledge of mathematics, science, engineering fundamentals, and an engineering specialization to the solution of complex engineering problems.\n\n\n**PO2:** Problem analysis: Identify, formulate, review research literature, and analyze complex engineering problems reaching substantiated conclusions using first principles of mathematics, natural sciences, and engineering sciences.\n\n\n\n**PO3:** Design/development of solutions: Design solutions for complex engineering problems and design system components or processes that meet the specified needs with appropriate consideration for the public health and safety, and the cultural, societal, and environmental considerations.\n\n\n**PO4:** Conduct investigations of complex problems: Use research-based knowledge and research methods including design of experiments, analysis and interpretation of data, and synthesis of the information to provide valid conclusions.\n\n\n\n**PO5:** Modern tool usage: Create, select, and apply appropriate techniques, resources, and modern engineering and IT tools including prediction and modeling to complex engineering activities with an understanding of the limitations.\n\n\n**PO6:** The engineer and society: Apply reasoning informed by the contextual knowledge to assess societal, health, safety, legal and cultural issues and the consequent responsibilities relevant to the professional engineering practice.\n\n\n**PO7:** Environment and sustainability: Understand the impact of the professional engineering solutions in societal and environmental contexts, and demonstrate the knowledge of, and need for sustainable development.\n\n\n\n**PO8:** Ethics: Apply ethical principles and commit to professional ethics and responsibilities and norms of the engineering practice.\n\n\n**PO9:** Individual and team work: Function effectively as an individual, and as a member or leader in diverse teams, and in multidisciplinary settings.\n\n\n**PO10:** Communication: Communicate effectively on complex engineering activities with the engineering community and with society at large, such as, being able to comprehend and write effective reports and design documentation, make effective presentations, and give and receive clear instructions.\n\n\n**PO11:** Project management and finance: Demonstrate knowledge and understanding of the engineering and management principles and apply these to one’s own work, as a member and leader in a team, to manage projects and in multidisciplinary environments.\n\n\n\n**PO12:** Life-long learning: Recognize the need for, and have the preparation and ability to engage in independent and life-long learning in the broadest context of technological change.\n\n\nPSO's\n\nThe following are the Program Specific Outcomes of Engineering Graduate:\n\n\n**PSO1:** Able to apply mathematical and advanced CAD tools required for design analysis and manufacturing products.\n\n\n\n**PSO2:** Getting employment in various industries and solving complex problems with systematic approach.\n\n\n\n**PSO3:** Apply innovative skills to lead as an entrepreneur or automobile researcher.\n\n\n![hero](https://sietk.org/images/faculty-imgs/mech-hod.png)\n\n# Dr.S.Sunil Kumar Reddy    Professor and HOD - Mechanical Department\n\nDr. S.Sunil Kumar Reddy obtained his B.Tech degree from Sri Venkateswara University, Tirupati, M.Tech and P.hD both from JNTUA, Ananthapuramu. He has a teaching experience of 24 years and worked in various prestigious Institutions in A.P. He conducted many number of national and International symposiums. He is acting as Single Point of Contact (SPOC) for the labs established by Siemens and Dassault companies along with APSSDC. He is trained in Applied Robotic control lab under the initiative of Indo-European Skilling cluster for Mechatronics and Manufacturing at Achen, Germany\n\n\nHe published nearly 65 research articles in National and International Journals and Conferences. His area of expertise is in Thermal Engineering, Combustion and Alternate Fuels. In his service he has guided more than 40 UG projects and 20 PG projects. He is a recognized research guide for JNTUA and Veltech Rangarajan Dr.Saguntala R&D Institute of Science and Technology, Chennai. Under him three Ph.D research scholars are working on Alternate fuels and Diesel engine Combustion. He is a Life Member of various professional societies like ISOC, NDT, SAE and Institution of Engineers.\n\n\n# REGULATIONS & SYLLABUS\n\nR23\n\n[Mechanical (R23) Complete syllabus](https://sietk.org/downloads/syllabus/UG/R23/R23%20MECH%20SYLLABUS.pdf)\n\nR20\n\n[Mechanical (R20) Complete syllabus](https://sietk.org/downloads/syllabus/UG/R20/R20%20ME%20For%20Website.pdf)\n\nR19\n\n[Mechanical (R19) Complete syllabus](https://sietk.org/downloads/syllabus/UG/R19/R19%20ME%20For%20Website.pdf)\n\nR18\n\n[Mechanical (R18) Complete syllabus](https://sietk.org/downloads/syllabus/UG/R18/R18%20ME%20For%20Website.pdf)\n\nR16\n\n[Mechanical (R16) Complete syllabus](https://sietk.org/downloads/syllabus/UG/R16/MECHR16.pdf)\n\n# Board of Studies Members (MECH)\n\n,\n\n\n| S.No | Member Name | Designation / Organization | Role of Bos | Category of Nomination |\n| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |\n| 1 | Dr.S.Sunil Kumar Reddy | HOD | Chairman | Head of the Department |\n| 2 | Dr. C. This will introduce a new idea, inspire students to further explore it on their own, or may illustrate and promote actual process practice.\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/subpages-imgs/Labs/melabs/mslab.png)\n\n## Material Science Lab:\n\nThe objective of a Materials science lab is to predict and control material properties through an understanding of atomic, molecular, crystalline, and microscopic structures of engineering materials. In this lab the students will prepare the sample workpiece and test them in microscopes for structures.\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/subpages-imgs/Labs/melabs/cadlab.png)\n\n## Computer Aided Design Lab:\n\nIn this lab the students will develop and analyze the designs of various mechanical components using 2D and 3D Software. The major software used in the lab is AUTOCAD/CATIA/DELMIA/SIMULIA. The basic knowledge of this can be used for successful accomplishment of project works.\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/subpages-imgs/Labs/melabs/mtlab.png)\n\n## Manufacturing Technology Lab:\n\nManufacturing Technology Laboratory is a well-equipped laboratory which provides ideas on the practical knowledge of several manufacturing processes used in the Industry. The major processes are casting, pattern usage, mould creation and welding.\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/subpages-imgs/Labs/melabs/telab.png)\n\n## Thermal Engineering Lab:\n\nIn this laboratory, students will have the opportunity to study the working principle of IC\nengines (both SI and CI engines), performance and characteristics,\neconomical speed variations, air fuel ratio influence on the engine. Here the student perform required tests, analyze subsequent data, and present the results in a professionally prepared report.\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/subpages-imgs/Labs/melabs/htlab.png)\n\n## Heat Transfer Lab:\n\nHeat Transfer laboratory provides fundamental and industrial knowledge about modes of heat transfer, like conduction, convection and radiation, and their application. In this the students will perform experiments on heat exchangers, boiling and condensation, Emissivity apparatus and Pin Fin Apparatus.\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/subpages-imgs/Labs/melabs/machinetoollab.png)\n\n## Machine Tools Lab:\n\nThis laboratory provides an introduction to the Know-how of common processes used in industries for manufacturing parts by removal of material in a controlled\nmanner. The emphasis throughout the laboratory course will be on understanding the basic features of the processes and acquiring skill in the operation of machines.\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/subpages-imgs/Labs/melabs/mmlab.png)\n\n## Metrology & Measurements Lab:\n\nThe objectives of this lab is to: Learn the main principle on which different instruments operate and provide hands on experience on them. Generate knowledge and skill in use of precision instruments. Learn a basic understanding of various instruments used in linear and angular measurements.\n\n# FACULTY ACHIVEMENTS\n\n# Department Infrastructure\n\n# Class Room Dimensions\n\n| S.No | Course | Particulars | Number of Rooms | Name of Room | L x B of the Per Class room in Meter | Per Class room in Meter Square | Total Carpet area of Room (sq.m) |\n| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |\n| 1 | B.Tech | Class Rooms | 10 | D-101, D-102, D-103, D-104, D-202, D-203, D-204, D-205, <br> D-302, D-303 | 8 \\* 9.10 | 72.8 | 651.81 |\n| 2 | B.Tech | Drawing Hall | 4 | D-301,D-402,D-404,<br> D-405 | 12.60 \\* 12.07 | 152.082 | 456.246 |\n| 3 | B.Tech | Tutorial rooms | 2 | D-306,D-307 | 5.93 \\* 9.10 | 53.963 | 107.926 |\n| 4 | B.Tech | Manufacturing Technology Lab | 1 | W-101 | 8.54 \\* 8.54 | 72.94 | 72.94 |\n| 5 | B.Tech | Material Sciences and Metallurgy Lab | 1 | W-102 | 8.54 \\* 8.54 | 72.94 | 72.94 |\n| 6 | B.Tech | Thermal Engineering- Lab | 1 | W-103 | 10.37 \\* 7.625 | 79.01 | 79.01 |\n| 7 | B.Tech | Heat Transfer Lab | 1 | W-104 | 11.9 \\* 6.405 | 76.1 | 76.1 |\n| 8 | B.Tech | Instrumentation and<br> control System and Metrology and Measurements | 1 | W-105 | 11.9 \\* 6.405 | 76.1 | 76.1 |\n| 9 | B.Tech | Machine Tools Lab | 1 | W-108 | 12.505 \\* 9.15 | 114.375 | 114.375 |\n| 10 | B.Tech | Engineering Workshops | 1 | W-109 | 23.77 \\* 8.54 | 202.9 | 202.9 |\n| 11 | B.Tech | CAD/CAE Lab | 1 | Design CBT Lab | 11.10 \\* 13.70 | 152.07 | 152.07 |\n| 12 | M.Tech | Thermal Engineering Class Rooms | 2 | D-302,D-303 | 8 \\* 9.10 | 72.8 | 145.6 |\n| 13 | M.Tech | Advanced CAD Lab | 2 | Dassault 3D Experience Center | 11.8 \\* 6.65 | 78.47 | 156.94 |\n|  |  |  | Grand Total | 2276.94 |\n\n# Seminar Hall\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/subpages-imgs/mech_new/infra/8.png)\n\n# Labs\n\n# AUTO 2 WHEELER LAB\n\nThis lab is established with the collaboration of APSSDC and SIEMENS company. In this lab the students will learn the 2 wheeler construction and repairing mechanisms. With this the students can able to repair their personal vehicles as and when needed.\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/subpages-imgs/mech_new/infra/1.png)\n\n# AUTO 4 WHEELER LAB\n\nThe main objective of 4 wheeler lab is to provide skill training in repairing mechanisms. With this the students can able to repair vehicles as and when needed and sustain in their life. This lab is established with the collaboration of APSSDC and SIEMENS company.\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/subpages-imgs/mech_new/infra/2.png)\n\n# REFRIGERATION & AIRCONDITIONING LAB\n\nThis lab is established with the collaboration of APSSDC and SIEMENS company. Refrigeration & Air Conditioning Lab gives idea on hands on experience with refrigerating circuits and develop air-conditioning systems. In this lab the students can able to identify and work with various kinds of refrigeration & Air-conditioning systems\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/subpages-imgs/mech_new/infra/3.png)\n\n# DESIGN CBT LAB\n\nIn this lab the students will develop and analyze the designs of various mechanical components using 2D and 3D Software. The major software used in the lab is SOLID EDGE. The basic knowledge of this can be used for successful accomplishment of project works. This lab is established with the collaboration of APSSDC and SIEMENS company.\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/subpages-imgs/mech_new/infra/4.png)\n\n# DASSAULT 3D EXPERIENCE CENTER\n\nThis lab is established with the coloration of APSSDC and Dassault Systemes company. The main aim of the lab is to develop and analyze the designs of various mechanical components using 2D and 3D Software. The major software used in the lab is AUTOCAD/CATIA/DELMIA/SIMULIA. This enable the students to accomplishment of project works.\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/subpages-imgs/mech_new/infra/5.png)\n\n# CM SKILL CENTER\n\nThis lab is established with the coloration of APSSDC. The main aim of the lab is to provide 2D and 3D software training to students on various platforms/software like AUTOCAD, ROBCAD, SOLID WORKS, PRO-E etc., to develop and analyze the designs of various mechanical components.\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/subpages-imgs/mech_new/infra/6.png)\n\n# Department Libruary\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/subpages-imgs/mech_new/infra/7.png)\n\n# Best Practices\n\n# Students\n\nStudent mentoring system\n\n\nEnvision and Execution by Association Activities\n\n\nRemedial classes for low performed students\n\n\nConducting guest lectures/seminars and workshops on cutting edge technologies\n\n\nConcept teaching with instructional models\n\n\nCreating awareness for higher studies, EDC, Placements etc.,\n\n\nSpecial training to students once the campus drive is planned\n\n\nRewarding the student toppers\n\n\nSkill oriented training will be provided to students\n\n\nRegular Internships and Industrial visits\n\n\n# Staff\n\nMotivating the staff to apply for funding projects\n\n\nEncouraging the staff for paper publications\n\n\nEncouraging the staff to participate in conferences, FDP and workshops\n\n\nEncouraging the staff for higher studies\n\n\n# Industry Integration\n\nThe department of mechanical engineering is integrated with various industries for the academic curriculum preparation, Internships and Industrial visits. Some of the companies installed industrial labs in the campus for the purpose of providing training to students on cutting edge technologies and make them industry ready or self-sustain in the Technology, Puttur, AndhraPradesh.. Enriched with 18 years of teaching experience, her profile has an assorted display of more than 50 papers in national and international journals. These papers cover a wide variety of significant topics ranging from Medical Image Processing, Wireless networks, FPGA based power systems, Digital Logic Design, Testing to Signal processing. She published various books on VLSI Design,Digital Image Processing, Embedded and IOT systems and Machine Learning Techniques. She also published around ten patents in Indian Patent System . She earned her Bachelor’s degree in Electronics and Communication Engineering at Mohamed Sathak Engineering College, Kilakarai. A Masters in VLSI Design at Anna University Regional Centre, Madurai. [PIO](https://sietk.org/pio_sietk.php)\n\n[AICTE-IDEA LAB](https://sietk.org/idea-lab.php)☰\n\n# DEPARTMENT OF ELECTRICAL & ELECTRONICS ENGINEERING\n\n![content](https://sietk.org/images/dept-imgs/eee1.jpg)\n\nAbout EEEVision & MissionAbout HODRegulations & SyllabusBoard of StudiesFacultyLaboratoryFaculty AcheivementsLectureNotes\n\n# ABOUT EEE DEPARTMENT\n\nThe department of ELECTRICAL AND ELECTRONICS ENGINEERING (EEE) has been playing a pioneering role in producing scientists and technologists of good caliber. EEE department is to create talented and socially responsible engineers to make a better India and, in turn, a better world.\n\nElectrical Engineers design systems that generate, transmit and distribute electricity. Electronics engineers design electronic devices which perform computation, communication, or control of robots and machines. Electrical and Electronics engineers work with technologies ranging from large power lines and generators to tiny integrated circuits containing billions of transistors.\n\n\nThe department has well-equipped laboratory facilities for the students such as Electrical Machine Lab, Basic Electrical and Network lab, Control & Instrumentation Lab, Power Electronics & Drives Lab with sophisticated equipment like dSPACE and Power Quality Analyser are available with the department. The infrastructure and lab facilities are upgraded from time to time and provide adequate opportunities for students to learn and innovate.\n\n\nElectrical and Electronics engineers are highly employable and can find work in many areas. An Electrical and Electronics engineer designs, develops and maintains the electrical, electronics and computer control system to the required specifications, and focusing on economy, reliability, safety, sustainability and quality. Telecom industries, transportation network, IT industries, airplane & airspace manufacturing industries, production and the distribution of power are some of the specific fields of career development. An Electrical and Electronics engineer can work with the industries deals in product development, control system, system management, product design, sales, consumer’s electronics, transportation, wireless communication, manufacturing, chemical, automotive, defense and space research organizations.\n\n\nInterested candidates can also build their career in teaching and research. They can join prestigious institutions for earning Master of Technology (M.Tech) degree and Ph.D degree in Electrical and Electronics Engineering.\n\n\nFounded in 2002, the Department of EEE has made rapid strides with the intake of 60, enhanced to 120 after four years. Till now 16 batches of students have graduated. The Department is headed by Dr. N.Ramesh Raju who has 21 years teaching experience & 4 Years Industrial Experience. The Department has competent, committed and well-qualified motivated faculty of 42 members possessing Ph.D and M.Tech. in various specializations.\n\n\n# VISION & MISSION OF THE DEPARTMENT\n\n## Vision\n\nTo produce competent Electrical & Electronics Engineering professionals through quality technical education and research and taking responsible positions to develop a value-based society.\n\n\n## Mission\n\nThe primary mission of the Department of Electrical and Electronics Engineering is to impart high class education to the students by its three tenets to serve the society:\n\nThe mission of the Department of Electric and Electronics Engineering has three tenets :\n\n**M1 :** Providing strong technical knowledge to formulate, solve, and analyze Electrical and Electronics Engineering problems.\n\n\n**M2 :** Collaborating with industry, research organizations, and academia to pursue research for the betterment of society.\n\n\n**M3 :** Preparing graduates with a positive attitude and ethical values for socio-economic growth and encouraging entrepreneurial ideas.\n\n\nPEO's\n\nProgram Educational Objectives (PEOs) are established by giving due consideration to the observations and expectations of the primary stakeholders. PEOs are broad statements that describe the career and professional accomplishments that the graduates should achieve within three to five years after the year of graduation.\n\n**PEO1:** To apply the fundamentals of science, engineering, and mathematics to solve Electrical Engineering and allied problems.\n\n\n**PEO2:** To solve industry problems with the help of software, testing, and design.\n\n\n**PEO3:** To involve in research, higher studies, and to become successful entrepreneurs.\n\n\nPSO's\n\n**PSO1:** Analysis of Power Quality: Ability to acquire and\nanalyze live power quality data using power quality\nanalyzer.\n\n\n**PSO2:** Electrical Hardware Design: Ability to develop\npower electronic controllers and devices using\nadvanced hardware tools.\n\n\n**PSO3:** Software Simulation: Ability to design, simulate, and\nanalyze the electrical machines and power systems\nthrough high-performance tools\n\n\n![hero](https://sietk.org/images/faculty-imgs/eee-hod.png)\n\n# N. Ramesh Raju    Professor & HOD - EEE Department\n\nDr. N. Ramesh Raju did Ph.D. in Control Systems from K.L. University, M.Tech. in Instrumentation from IIT Kharagpur and B.Tech in Electronics and Instrumentation from KITS Warangal. He has 21 years of teaching experience and 4 years of industrial experience in Tata Electric Company, Bombay and Sterelite Industries India Ltd. ( Copper Smelter ) Tuticorin.\n\n\nHis research interests are Optimal Self Tuning of PID and Fractional Order PID Controllers, Applications of Soft Computing Techniques to Control Systems.\n\n\n# Outstroke during $6 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation;\n\n2. Dwell for the next $3 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation;\n\n\nL2 CO5 12M\n\n3. Return stroke during next $6 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation, and\n\n4. Dwell for the remaining $2 1 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation.\n\n\nThe stroke of the follower is $4 0 \\ \\\\mathrm { m m }$ and the minimum radius of the cam is $5 0 ~ \\\\mathrm { m m }$ . The follower moves with uniform velocity during both the outstroke and return strokes. Draw the profile of the cam when the axis of the follower is offset by $2 0 ~ \\\\mathrm { m m }$ from the axis of the cam shaft.\n\nA cam drives a flat reciprocating follower in the following manner: During first $1 2 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ rotation of the cam, follower moves outwards through a distance of $2 0 \\ \\\\mathrm { m m }$ with simple harmonic motion. The follower dwells during next $3 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation.\n\nL2 CO5 12M\n\nDuring next $1 2 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation, the follower moves inwards with simple harmonic motion. The follower dwells for the next $9 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation. The minimum radius of the cam is $2 5 ~ \\\\mathrm { m m }$ . Draw the profile of the cam.\n\n5 A Explain with sketches the different types of followers. b Write short notes on cams\n\n6 What are the different types of motion and how the follower can move in it?\n\n7 a Draw the displacement, velocity and acceleration diagrams for a follower when it moves with simple harmonic motion. b Draw the displacement, velocity and acceleration diagrams for a follower when it moves with uniform Acceleration and retardation.\n\nL2 CO5 6M\n\nDesign a cam for operating the exhaust valve of an oil engine. It is required to give equal uniform acceleration and retardation during opening and closing of the valve each of which corresponds to $6 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation. The valve must remain in\n\nthe fully open position for $2 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation. The lift of the valve is $3 7 . 5 ~ \\\\mathrm { m m }$ and the least radius of the cam is $4 0 ~ \\\\mathrm { m m }$ . The follower is provided with a roller of radius $2 0 \\\\mathrm { m m }$ and its line of DHARTH stroke passes through the axis of the cam.\n\nA cam rotating clockwise at a uniform speed of 1000 r.p.m. is required to give a roller follower the motion defined below :\n\n1. Follower to move outwards through $5 0 \\\\mathrm { m m }$ during $1 2 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation,\n\n2. Follower to dwell for next $6 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation,\n\n3. Follower to return to its starting position during next $9 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation,\n\n4. Follower to dwell for the rest of the cam rotation.\n\n\nThe minimum radius of the cam is $5 0 \\ \\\\mathrm { m m }$ and the diameter of roller is $1 0 ~ \\\\mathrm { m m }$ . The line of stroke of the follower is off-set by $2 0 ~ \\\\mathrm { m m }$ from the axis of the cam shaft. If the displacement of the follower takes place with uniform and equal acceleration and retardation on both the outward and return strokes, draw profile\n\nL2 CO5 12M\n\nof the cam and find the maximum velocity and acceleration during out stroke and return stroke.\n\nIt is required to set out the profile of a cam to give the following motion to the reciprocating follower with a flat mushroom contact face :\n\n(i) Follower to have a stroke of $2 0 \\ \\\\mathrm { \\ m m }$ during $1 2 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation\n\n(ii) Follower to dwell for $3 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation ;\n\n(iii) Follower to return to its initial position during $1 2 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation ; and\n\n(iv) Follower to dwell for remaining $9 0 ^ { \\\\circ }$ of cam rotation.\n\nThe minimum radius of the cam is $2 5 ~ \\\\mathrm { m m }$ . The out stroke of the follower is performed with simple harmonic motion and the return stroke with equal uniform acceleration and retardation.\n\n# UNIT – V\n\n1. a Explain the terms :(i) Module, (ii) Pressure angle, and (iii) L2 CO6 6M\n\nb State and prove the law of gearing.
